# üúÇ **OVAC ‚Äî Implementation Blueprint**

OVAC is **a federated governance council**, not a tech stack by itself.
It *runs on process, infrastructure, and artifact pipelines* that your federation already has:

üîπ **Archive OS** ‚Äî immutable data storage
üîπ **Bahari Network** ‚Äî federation API / event bus
üîπ **Decision Tables** ‚Äî executable policy logic
üîπ **Entity Systems** ‚Äî identity, analytics, compliance units
üîπ **Shared Service Infrastructure** ‚Äî communications, calendaring, orchestration

OVAC is implemented by *activating governance artifact flows* rather than building a monolithic organization.

---

# ‚úÖ **1) Implementation Layers (What Actually Runs OVAC)**

### üîπ **Governance Infrastructure**

* **Archive OS** ‚Äî every OVAC artifact is stored and linked
* **Bahari Network** ‚Äî federation message transport
* **Decision Table Engine** ‚Äî executable policies and escalation logic
* **Artifact Repositories** ‚Äî structured flows of meetings/minutes

### üîπ **People Infrastructure**

OVAC seats are filled by:

* Board Reps (Class C)
* System Strategy Stewards
* Community Delegates (Class D)
* Independent Risk/Ethics Voices

These participants are *people*, but their activities are bound to governance processes and tools.

### üîπ **Process Infrastructure**

OVAC runs through *standardized workflows* and artifact lifecycles:

* Intake ‚Üí Pre-Review ‚Üí Deliberation ‚Üí Decision ‚Üí Implementation ‚Üí PIR
* Each step produces artifacts indexed in Archive OS

---

# ‚úÖ **2) What It Means for an Entity to *Host* OVAC**

When an entity hosts OVAC:

üëâ They take on **operational stewardship** of the OVAC governance machine for a rotation period.

Hosting is *not just convening people* ‚Äî it‚Äôs standing up the **service and data infrastructure that makes OVAC *work as a system*.**

---

## üß† **Hosting Responsibilities (Concrete)**

### **A. Deploy OVAC Service Bundle**

Each host entity must implement these services:

| Component                    | Implementation Task                                               |
| ---------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **OVAC Secretariat Service** | Calendaring, agenda publishing, minutes capture, artifact tagging |
| **Archive OS Integration**   | Ensure artifacts are versioned, decisionRef‚Äôd, and linked         |
| **Bahari Event Handler**     | A federation API endpoint for OVAC messages/requests              |
| **Decision Table Bindings**  | Enable metrics & triggers relevant to active memos                |
| **Governance UI/Portal**     | Dashboard for OVAC review queues, voting status, policies         |

**Deployment Checklist**

* Establish OVAC governance namespace in Archive OS
* Set up authorized Bahari API endpoints for OVAC artifacts
* Configure decision table modules relevant to active governance domains
* Provision dashboards and alerting channels for council actions

> These are *software-enabled governance capabilities*, not custom code ‚Äî they leverage your existing Pamoja platform stack.

---

### **B. Operational Secretariat**

The host entity must provide:

1. **Meeting Coordination Workflow**

   * Schedule sessions
   * Distribute agendas
   * Capture resolutions

2. **Artifact Publishing Workflows**

   * Minutes saved in Archive OS
   * Decision records linked to decisionRefs
   * Risk & pre-review artifacts attached

3. **Member Lifecycle Support**

   * Onboarding/offboarding of OVAC delegates
   * Access management via ZULAMBA identity services

**Artifacts Produced**

```
ovac.session.log
ovac.minutes.artifact
ovac.decision.record
```

These are governed by policies and archived immutably.

---

### **C. Federation Integration Adapters**

Hosting includes coordinating with federation service pods:

| Pod                  | What Host Must Do                                    |
| -------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| **ZULAMBA Identity** | Ensure OVAC delegates are authorized and role-mapped |
| **Ubuntuwa Commons** | Integrate legitimacy signals into memos              |
| **Uhuru CU**         | Link financial viability assessments                 |
| **Moyo**             | Provide human impact projections                     |
| **Archive Office**   | Archive artifacts                                    |
| **Bahari Network**   | Federation delivery and subscription routing         |

This makes OVAC *a true governance integrator*, not a siloed board.

IF financial.risk > threshold AND legitimacy.score < threshold

risk.assessment.artifact

‚Üí returns chain of linked artifacts

# ‚úÖ **7) GOVERNANCE & EXECUTABLE DECISION TABLES**

OVAC uses **executable decision tables** to align decisions with doctrine:

Examples:

```
IF (value_alignment >= 80%) AND (risk < medium)
THEN APPROVE

IF (financial_risk >= high) AND (legitimacy_score < threshold)
THEN DEFER + REQUEST MITIGATIONS
```

This makes governance:

* **Deterministic**
* **Auditable**
* **Executable**
* **Traceable**

Below is a **clear, practical explanation** of what **‚Äúpods‚Äù are** in your OVAC governance model ‚Äî and a **step-by-step operational narrative** of how OVAC will *actually work and be implemented by federation entities over a year*.

This is *specific to your Pamoja ecosystem*, not generic corporate governance.

---

# üß† **What Are ‚ÄúPods‚Äù in OVAC Context?**

**Pods** are *functional service units* that support OVAC by supplying domain-specific inputs, analysis, signals, and risk/context assessments.

Think of them like **specialized advisory & operational cells** that feed structured information into the OVAC decision pipeline.

Each pod is *not OVAC itself* ‚Äî but rather a **service provider for OVAC**, meaning they produce artifacts used during deliberation.

Pods may be *standing teams* (like internal services) or *federated cooperative clusters* (like Ubuntuwa Commons, ZULAMBA, Moyo, etc.)

---

## üß≠ **Core Pods (Your Federation Version)**

| **Pod Name**                        | **Primary Purpose**                                                                        |
| ----------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Identity & Authority Pod**        | Ensures member identity, role legitimacy, and authority mappings for decision eligibility. |
| **Legitimacy & Social Signals Pod** | Supplies Ubuntuwa legitimacy scores and narrative coherence analysis.                      |
| **Financial/Capital Pod**           | Provides financial risk, viability, and budget analysis (e.g., Uhuru CU inputs).           |
| **Human Systems Pod**               | Provides human impact metrics and resilience indicators (via Moyo).                        |
| **Continuity & Succession Pod**     | Assesses continuity risks and succession readiness.                                        |
| **Integration & Tech Ops Pod**      | Ensures API/Archive OS/Bahari integration and technical compliance signals.                |
| **Compliance & Ethics Pod**         | Assesses regulatory, ethical, privacy, and risk compliance signals.                        |

Each pod *produces artifacts* ‚Äî structured, tagged data objects that OVAC uses during deliberation.

Artifacts include:

```
legitimacy.score
identity.validation.artifact
financial.risk.report
human.impact.index
continuity.readiness.map
compliance.status.artifact
```

These artifacts are linked to decisions via:

```
decisionRef IDs
```

# üìÖ **Operational Narrative ‚Äî How OVAC Works Over a Year**

The following narrative assumes a **Year-1 operational cycle** with typical federation activity.

---

## **‚öôÔ∏è Year Start ‚Äî OVAC Host Activation**

### **Entities prepare to host OVAC (by schedule):**

Example: Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA Coalition is Year-Start Host.

### **Host does:**

1. **Provision OVAC infrastructure**

   * Set up Archive OS namespaces
   * Register Bahari endpoints for OVAC
   * Configure decision tables relevant for the year

2. **Initialize secretary support**

   * Calendars, collaboration channels, documentation standards

3. **Onboard/offboard OVAC members**

   * Update ZULAMBA identity roles for incoming council members

Artifacts created:

```
ovac.host.initialized
ovac.member.onboarded (per member)
```

---

## **üßæ Month 1 ‚Äî Intake & Planning**

OVAC opens the year by:

* Reviewing pending investment proposals
* Updating doctrine references
* Syncing pod thresholds and risk criteria

Pods produce baseline signals:

* Identity & Authority validation
* Social legitimacy baselines
* Financial baseline reports
* Human systems baseline reports

Artifacts:

```
baseline.legitimacy.score
financial.baseline.report
human.baseline.metrics
```

---

## **üì© Regular Operations ‚Äî OVAC Intake Pipeline**

### **Scenario:** A federation entity submits an **Investment Memo**.

**Step 1 ‚Äî Submission**

* Entity submits via Archive OS ‚Üí tagged as `ovac.request`
* Bahari Network routes receipt event
* Host portal shows incoming queue

Artifact:

```
ovac.request.created
```

**Step 2 ‚Äî Triage**

* Secretariat assigns:

  * Which pods to consult
  * Priority based on request size/risk
* Decision table assigns triage category

Artifact:

```
ovac.request.triaged
```

**Step 3 ‚Äî Pod Reviews**
Each pod contributes artifacts:

* Identity Pod: verifies authority permission

  ```
  identity.validation.artifact
  ```
* Legitimacy Pod: Ubuntuwa legitimacy score

  ```
  legitimacy.score.artifact
  ```
* Financial Pod: Uhuru CU financial risk

  ```
  financial.risk.report
  ```
* Human Systems Pod: Moyo human impact

  ```
  human.impact.index
  ```
* Continuity Pod: continuity risk analysis

  ```
  continuity.readiness.map
  ```

These feed into OVAC‚Äôs unified review packet.

---

## **üó£Ô∏è Deliberation & Sleepy Consensus**

OVAC synthesizes pod artifacts into a **decision packet**.

Using *sleepy consensus*, members may:

‚úî Endorse
‚úî Raise a concern
‚úî Ask for conditions
‚úî Block (if critical risk)

If no blocking within the consensus window (e.g., 72h), OVAC proceeds.

Artifacts:

```
ovac.decision.draft
ovac.consensus.log
```

---

## **üìä Decision & Archive OS**

Final decision is:

* Approved
* Approved with conditions
* Deferred
* Rejected

Each decision references:

* Attached artifacts
* Conditions
* Escalation triggers

Artifact:

```
ovac.decision.record
```

This feeds:

```
decisionRef ‚Üí implementation.plan
```

---

## **üì¶ Implementation & Monitoring**

Once approved:

* Entity implements plan
* Quarterly reports are submitted

  ```
  implementation.q1.report
  ```
* Nodes update progress
* Risk monitors track KPI shifts

Artifacts:

```
progress.artifact
risk.escalation.log
```

If thresholds breach:

* Automated escalation via decision tables

  ```
  escalation.triggered
  ```

---

## **üìâ Mid-Year Review**

OVAC conducts a midyear review:

* KPI trends
* Doctrine updates
* Pod threshold adjustments

Artifacts:

```
midyear.review.artifact
decisionTable.update
```

---

## **üìë Post-Implementation Review (PIR)**

At project end:

* OVAC reviews outcomes
* Updates decision tables as needed
* Lessons learned are archived

Artifacts:

```
post.implementation.review
lesson.learned.artifact
```

---

# üß† **Concrete Example ‚Äî Investment Request Lifecycle**

**Entity:** Moyo Collective submits Year-1 business plan
**Use Case:** OVAC must decide on approval

**Flow:**

1. *Submit* ‚Üí Archive OS `ovac.request`
2. *Triage* ‚Üí Tags: Pods: Identity, Legitimacy, Finance, Human Systems, Continuity
3. *Pod Reviews* ‚Üí artifacts created
4. *OVAC Consensus* ‚Üí Sleepy consensus over 72h
5. *Decision* ‚Üí `ovac.decision.record`

   * Condition: Quarterly check-ins
6. *Implementation* ‚Üí Pod monitors track signals
7. *PIR* ‚Üí Analytics confirm impacts

Every step is traceable.

---

# üß© **Why This Works**

üü¢ **Distributed accountability** ‚Äî No single entity controls OVAC
üü¢ **Asynchronous governance** ‚Äî Sleepy consensus reduces meetings
üü¢ **Artifact traceability** ‚Äî Every input/output is logged
üü¢ **Pod specialization** ‚Äî Complex decisions are informed by domain experts
üü¢ **Decision tables + thresholds** ‚Äî Operational governance is executable and auditable

| --------------------------- | --------------------------------------- | ------------------------ |
| **Identity & Authority**    | Validates who can sign + act            | identity.validation      |
| **Legitimacy & Social**     | Social acceptance & narrative alignment | legitimacy.score         |

| **Human Systems**           | Member impact & resilience              | human.impact.index       |
| **Continuity & Succession** | Long-term stability risk                | continuity.readiness.map |
| **Compliance & Ethics**     | Regulatory & doctrinal conformity       | compliance.status        |
| **Integration & Tech Ops**  | Ensures artifacts flow                  | integration.health       |

**Morning:**

* New requests logged
* Secretariat updates request queue
* Identity pod verifies delegates

**Midday:**

* Pods submit review artifacts
* Host prepares decision packets

**Afternoon:**

* OVAC members review asynchronously
* Sleepy consensus window begins

**Evening:**

* If no blocks, decision is issued
* Implementation plans are routed via Bahari

**Next Day:**

* Progress dashboards updated

Below is a **practical, step-by-step implementation plan** for how to **set up OVAC** from *Day 0 when you launch your Kernel Organization (your personal estate) and the first core entities (OVCS, Kumba, your personal office), *all the way through** the emergence of the Pamoja Federation and the Ashe cycle.

This is a **programmatic governance and implementation narrative** ‚Äî not abstract ‚Äî so you can put it into practice in your docs, systems, or operations.

---

# üöÄ THE BIG PICTURE

You are bootstrapping:

1. **Your Kernel Organization** (Dominic Eaton‚Äôs personal estate + office)
2. The first three core operational entities:

   * **Obatala Venture Capital Studios (OVCS)**
   * **Kumba Metafactory**
   * **Your Personal Office (Navigator HQ)**
3. From these, the rest of the **Pamoja Federation** ‚Äî Ubuntuwa, ZULAMBA, Uhuru, Moyo, Bahari, etc.

**OVAC (Operational & Value-Alignment Council)** does *not exist at Day 0*, but it is **programmatically instantiated early once there is enough cross-entity governance complexity** ‚Äî usually when multi-entity proposals, capital allocations, or shared doctrine decisions are required.

OVAC is a **governance system**, not just a committee; it comes alive as the federation grows and needs a governance backbone.

---

## üß© WHY OVAC MATTERS EARLY

OVAC isn‚Äôt ‚Äúnice to have‚Äù ‚Äî it ensures that:

‚úî Multi-entity investment decisions are aligned
‚úî Doctrine is applied consistently
‚úî Risk and social legitimacy are integrated
‚úî Shared service dependencies are governed
‚úî Cross-organizational initiatives are decided fairly
‚úî Continuity & succession plans are baked into strategic decisions

In other words:
**As soon as more than one entity needs to make shared decisions with capital or strategic risk, OVAC must be in place.**

# üõ†Ô∏è STEP-BY-STEP IMPLEMENTATION GUIDE

Below is the **operational process you would follow** as you build out your federation and bring OVAC online.

---

## üóìÔ∏è **PHASE 0 ‚Äî DAY ZERO: KERNEL ORGANIZATION SETUP**

**Context:**
Your personal estate exists; you have core identity, personal office, and the first entities: **OVCS** and **Kumba**.

**Goal:**
Start governance infrastructure without activating OVAC fully.

---

### üìå Tasks

**1. Define Doctrine & Foundational Decision Tables**
Establish a minimal doctrine system that will eventually scale into OVAC governance, with decision tables such as:

* Investment governance rules
* Authority & identity rules
* Conflict escalation rules
* Continuity & succession rules

These initial decision tables can be hosted in:

```
Archive OS
```

(immutable, auditable storage).

---

**2. Stand Up Core Entity Governance Structures**
For each initial entity:

* OVCS ‚Äî define governance charter, investment review process
* Kumba ‚Äî define build/operational charter
* Personal Office ‚Äî define strategic oversight role

These charters include *references to doctrine*, but OVAC is not fully active yet.

---

**3. Establish Identity & Master Profiles**
Use **ZULAMBA logic** early (even if ZULAMBA itself isn‚Äôt launched):

* Create master identity for your Kernel Organization
* Assign role classes (Your personal estate = Class E Founder; OVCS board = Class C, etc.)

This sets up identity foundations.

---

**4. Prepare Archive OS & Bahari Infrastructure**

* Configure artifact namespaces
* Set up integration patterns for events
* Decide how future governance artifacts will be stored and indexed
* Ensure all three initial entities can write and read shared artifacts

No OVAC yet ‚Äî but the infrastructure is ready.

---

## üóìÔ∏è **PHASE 1 ‚Äî MULTI-ENTITY INTERACTIONS BEGIN**

**Trigger:**
More than one entity starts interacting in shared decisions. For example:

* OVCS requests investment capital
* Kumba wants operational funding
* Your personal office needs approval for cross-entity strategic decisions

At this point, **OVAC processes kick in.**

---

## üü° **WHEN TO ACTIVATE OVAC**

**OVAC should be instantiated when:**

üîπ Two or more independent organizational entities need to make a *joint decision*
üîπ Capital allocation across entities is required
üîπ A doctrine decision affects entity interoperability
üîπ Strategic policy needs review beyond a single entity
üîπ A cross-entity risk surface emerges

For a federation, this generally happens when:

* OVCS issues a **Joint Venture Proposal**
* Kumba needs **capital for a shared build**
* Your personal office initiates **federated doctrine updates**

At this point the governance design transitions from *entity-specific committee* to **OVAC governance flows**.

---

## üõ†Ô∏è **ACTIVATING OVAC ‚Äî STEP BY STEP**

### üö© 1. **Define OVAC Host Entity**

Pick an initial host from the federation ‚Äî usually:

‚û° **Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA Coalition**
or
‚û° **Your personal office (if there is no Ubuntuwa yet)**

The host entity provides:

* Secretariat operations
* Meeting facilitation
* Artifact publication pipelines
* Bahari Network integration endpoints

Host responsibility is formalized with:

```
ovac.host.charter.artifact
```

---

### üö© 2. **Nominate OVAC Members**

Populate OVAC from founding class pools:

* Board Reps (Class C) ‚Äî OVCS board, Kumba board
* Strategy Stewards ‚Äî eg: You + senior leadership
* Community Delegates ‚Äî future Ubuntuwa Commons reps
* Independent Counsel/Risk ‚Äî external advisor tokens

Publish nominees:

```
ovac.members.nomination
ovac.member.onboarded
```

---

### üö© 3. **Onboard OVAC Delegates**

Each delegate is:

* Identity-verified (ZULAMBA)
* Given access to Archive OS artifacts
* Added to Bahari federated message groups
* Assigned roles via decision tables

Artifacts:

```
ovac.member.onboarding
```

---

### üö© 4. **Define OVAC Processes**

OVAC needs executable governance flows:

* Investment Request process
* Policy Amendment process
* Entity Charter addition
* Risk Escalation process
* Crisis decision process

Implement these via **decision tables and governance rules**, such as:

```
IF funding_request > threshold
THEN require OVAC review
```

---

### üö© 5. **Stand Up Secretariat & Tooling**

The host entity configures:

* Calendar and governance ritual schedule
* Bahari RPC/Webhooks for requests
* Archive OS schema for OVAC artifacts
* Dashboards for requests & decisions

Artifacts:

```
ovac.host.initialized
ovac.request.queue
ovac.session.schedule
```

---

## üóìÔ∏è **PHASE 2 ‚Äî FIRST OVAC CYCLE**

### üîπ **First OVAC Intake**

Entities submit their first governance artifact (e.g., OVCS investment memo). OVAC will:

1. **Receive the request**

   * Through Archive OS + Bahari event
   * Tagged with entity sponsor

2. **Triage with pods**

   * Identity & Authority
   * Legitimacy (Ubuntuwa)
   * Financial (Uhuru)
   * Human impact (Moyo)
   * Continuity & Risk

Each pod returns a structured artifact.

3. **Deliberate via sleepy consensus**

   * Review packet assembled
   * Sleepy consensus window opens (asynchronous)
   * Critical objections escalate to synchronous session

4. **Issue Decision**

   * Approved / Conditional / Deferred / Rejected
   * Logged to Archive OS
   * Decision conditions attached

Artifacts:

```
ovac.decision.record
decision.conditions
```

---

## üóìÔ∏è **PHASE 3 ‚Äî FEEDBACK & CONTINUITY**

After the first cycle, OVAC:

* Tracks implementation progress
* Coordinates quarterly check-ins
* Watches risk thresholds
* Updates decision tables as needed

Artifacts:

```
implementation.status
quarterly.progress.report
risk.summary.artifact
```

OVAC becomes crucial when:

üìå An entity (e.g., OVCS) seeks multi-entity capital
üìå Kumba proposes federated manufacturing infrastructure
üìå Doctrine updates impact identity/legal structures
üìå Risk surfaces emerge across human systems
üìå Policies need federation-wide alignment

OVAC is *the governance mechanism* that ensures:

* **Legitimacy**
* **Alignment**
* **Risk control**
* **Continuity**
* **Traceability**
* **Doctrine conformity**

Each pod is *not OVAC* but a *dependency of the governance pipeline* that OVAC harnesses.

**Short answer:**
‚úÖ **Yes ‚Äî in your ecosystem, OVAC functions as the Pamoja Federation‚Äôs *federation-level board-like authority*** ‚Äî but it‚Äôs *not just a ‚Äúboard‚Äù in the traditional corporate sense*. It‚Äôs a **governance council with specific doctrinal, alignment, risk, and strategic authority** that sits *above* individual coop boards and coordinates shared decisions across the federation.

Here‚Äôs what that means in practice:

---

# üúÇ **What OVAC *Is***

OVAC (**O**perational & **V**alue-**A**lignment **C**ouncil) is:

üîπ A **federation governance authority**
üîπ A **decision-making council**
üîπ A **doctrinal alignment body**
üîπ A **shared supervision layer** for cross-entity issues
üîπ A **board-like institution** for federation-wide strategy

It is *not* merely another coop board ‚Äî it‚Äôs the body that:

* Ensures cross-entity decisions *align with federation doctrine and values*
* Reviews and approves investment memos and multi-entity proposals
* Integrates signals from identity, legitimacy, risk, continuity, and financial pods
* Sets federation-wide priorities and investment standards
* Coordinates major policy, resource, and risk decisions

In that sense, **it *is* the federation‚Äôs ‚Äúboard of boards‚Äù** ‚Äî a *meta-governance body*.

---

# üß† **How OVAC Relates to Coop Boards**

Your federation has many coop boards (e.g., OVCS board, Kumba board, Ubuntuwa boards, etc.). Each coop has:

‚úî Legal authority over its own entity
‚úî Responsibility for entity-specific strategy
‚úî Decision rights within its domain

But when a decision:

üî∏ Affects **multiple coops**, or
üî∏ Requires **shared resources**, or
üî∏ Impacts the **whole federation‚Äôs legitimacy or capital**, or
üî∏ Is a **federation doctrine matter**‚Ä¶

‚Ä¶it crosses the boundary where a single coop board **no longer has the final say**.

That‚Äôs where **OVAC steps in**.

OVAC is the *governance level that sits above and coordinates individual coop boards* for federation-wide alignment.

---

# üìä **OVAC vs Coop Board ‚Äî What‚Äôs the Difference?**

| Feature        | Coop Board (Entity-level)              | OVAC (Federation-level)                                                      |
| -------------- | -------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Scope          | Single entity                          | Multi-entity / federation                                                    |
| Authority      | Entity charter & bylaws                | Federation doctrine & alignment                                              |
| Decisions      | Internal governance, budgets, policies | Shared resource allocation, cross-entity strategy, doctrine enforcement      |
| Inputs         | Entity KPIs                            | Multidimensional signals (identity, legitimacy, finance, risk, continuity)   |
| Members        | Board reps for one coop                | Representatives across classes (C, D, strategy stewards, independent voices) |
| Decision Logic | Entity policies                        | Federation decision tables + doctrine                                        |

---

# üß© **OVAC‚Äôs Governance Role in the Federation**

OVAC is designed to do things **coop boards can‚Äôt or shouldn‚Äôt do on their own**, such as:

### üü° **1. Approve Multi-Entity Investments**

When an investment affects more than one coop (e.g., a cross-coop venture), OVAC reviews the investment memo and authorizes capital deployment.

### üü° **2. Resolve Cross-Entity Conflicts**

If two or more coops have conflicting strategies, risk priorities, or resource allocations, OVAC mediates and decides.

### üü° **3. Interpret & Apply Doctrine**

OVAC ensures that all federation actions conform to agreed doctrines and values ‚Äî codified in decision tables.

### üü° **4. Integrate Signals from Pods**

OVAC consumes inputs from:

* **Identity/Authority Pod (ZULAMBA)**
* **Legitimacy & Narrative (Ubuntuwa)**
* **Financial Risk (Uhuru)**
* **Human Systems (Moyo)**
* **Continuity & Succession**
* **Compliance & Ethics**
  ‚Ä¶and makes decisions based on combined signals.

### üü° **5. Maintain Continuity & Resilience**

OVAC oversees federation-wide continuity planning, crisis response, and governance stability ‚Äî especially when entities have leadership changes or shock events.

---

# üß† **OVAC as ‚ÄúFederation Board‚Äù ‚Äî But With a Governance Architecture**

It *is board-like*, but with **structured governance mechanics**:

### ‚úî **Decision Tables**

Executable governance logic that codifies doctrine and reduces arbitrariness.

### ‚úî **Sleepy Consensus Model**

A federated consensus mechanism that fits distributed part-time governance without requiring constant quorum.

### ‚úî **Pods**

Functional units that supply structured analysis into OVAC (identity, legitimacy, finance, human systems, continuity, compliance).

### ‚úî **Archive OS**

Immutable storage and traceability for all governance artifacts ‚Äî decisions, conditions, votes, signals, reviews.

### ‚úî **Bahari Network**

Federation-wide message/transport layer for artifacts and signals.

---

# üß† **How OVAC Works in Practice (High Level)**

1. A federation-wide proposal, investment memo, or doctrine change is submitted.
2. Pods generate structured signals (identity authority checks, legitimacy scores, financial risk, human impact).
3. OVAC convenes (synchronous or async via sleepy consensus).
4. Council reviews all artifacts and signals ‚Äî applying decision tables.
5. OVAC issues a decision (Approve, Conditional, Defer, Reject) with archived rationale.
6. Entities implement under OVAC conditions and report progress.
7. OVAC monitors implementation and risk via ongoing artifact streams.

---

# üìå **In Plain Terms ‚Äî Yes:**

**OVAC is essentially your federation‚Äôs cooperative board of oversight and alignment.**
But it is **broader than a single entity board** ‚Äî it is the *federation-wide governance council* that:

* Reviews cross-entity strategic decisions
* Applies shared doctrine
* Integrates multidomain risk & legitimacy signals
* Allocates resources across coops
* Ensures continuity and alignment of the federation

It *plays the role* of a federation board ‚Äî but it is **structured, distributed, doctrinal, and artifact-driven** rather than hierarchical or centralized.

---

## üßæ **1) OVAC Decision Table Framework (Executable Logic)**

This is a **modular decision table template** you can implement directly in your decision engine (or as JSON/CSV inputs). It covers common OVAC approval paths.

> Each row is an evaluation rule; the ‚ÄúOutcome‚Äù drives the next step.
> Columns tie to signals produced by pods (legitimacy, finance, continuity, etc.).

---

### **Decision Table: OVAC Approval ‚Äî Strategic Request**

| **Rule ID** | **Criteria**             | **Condition**                                | **Action / Outcome** | **Next Stage**                   |
| ----------- | ------------------------ | -------------------------------------------- | -------------------- | -------------------------------- |
| R1          | **Authority Check**      | identity.isAuthorized == `false`             | REJECT               | Notify Entity: Authority Missing |
| R2          | **Legitimacy Threshold** | legitimacy.score < LEG_MIN                   | DEFER                | Request Social Impact Plan       |
| R3          | **Financial Viability**  | financial.riskLevel >= HIGH                  | DEFER                | Ask for Revised Fiscal Plan      |
| R4          | **Continuity Readiness** | continuity.readiness == LOW                  | CONDITIONAL          | Require Continuity Mitigations   |
| R5          | **Human Impact Risk**    | human.impactIndex > RISK_THRESHOLD           | CONDITIONAL          | Add Human Systems Safeguards     |
| R6          | **Compliance Gate**      | compliance.status != PASS                    | DEFER                | Fix Compliance Issues            |
| R7          | **All Green Flags**      | legit ‚â• OK & finance ‚â§ MED & continuity ‚â• OK | APPROVE              | Issue Decision & Deploy Plan     |
| R8          | **Blocking Risk Flag**   | blockingRisk == TRUE                         | ESCALATE             | Immediate Council Review         |

---

## üßæ **Decision Table: Commentary / Usage Notes**

* **identity.isAuthorized** is typically provided by the *Identity & Authority Pod*.
* **legitimacy.score** comes from Ubuntuwa (social legitimacy + narrative alignment).
* **financial.riskLevel** is produced by the *Financial/Capital Pod* (e.g., Uhuru).
* **continuity.readiness** is provided by *Continuity & Succession Pod*.
* **human.impactIndex** is provided by *Human Systems Pod* (Moyo).
* **compliance.status** is from *Compliance & Ethics Pod*.
* **blockingRisk** is a synthesized flag when any core pod indicates a *hard stop* risk.

---

## üß† Operational Interpretation

‚úî If **any authority or compliance block exists**, OVAC should not approve.
‚úî If legitimacy or financial concerns exist, the proposal is *deferred with instructions*.
‚úî If continuity or human risk is moderate, approval can be *conditional*.
‚úî **Only when all signals pass thresholds** does OVAC approve.

This table is intended to be **machine-executable** and also readable by humans.

---

## üìà **2) Workflow Diagram ‚Äî OVAC Intake ‚Üí Decision ‚Üí Implementation**

Below is a **Mermaid diagram** that illustrates the entire governance pipeline from request intake to implementation and closing the loop.

You can render this in tools that support Mermaid (e.g., Markdown editors, governance dashboards in Notion/Obsidian, or federation portals).

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    subgraph Submission & Intake
        A[Entity Submission] --> B{Is Submission Complete?}
        B -- No --> A1[Return to Entity w/ Feedback]
        B -- Yes --> C[Register Request in Archive OS]
    end

    subgraph Pre-Review Pods
        C --> D1[Identity & Authority Pod]
        C --> D2[Legitimacy & Narrative Pod]
        C --> D3[Financial / Capital Pod]
        C --> D4[Human Systems Pod]
        C --> D5[Continuity & Succession Pod]
        C --> D6[Compliance & Ethics Pod]
    end

    subgraph OVAC Deliberation
        D1 --> E[Assemble Review Packet]
        D2 --> E
        D3 --> E
        D4 --> E
        D5 --> E
        D6 --> E
        E --> F{Sleepy Consensus Window}
        F -->|Consensus Reached| G[Execute Decision Table]
        F -->|Block / Objection| H[Escalate to Synchronous Session]
        H --> G
    end

    subgraph Decision Outcome
        G --> I{Decision Type}
        I --> |Approve| J[Approve + Conditions?]
        I --> |Conditional| K[Return Conditions to Entity]
        I --> |Defer| L[Request Revision]
        I --> |Reject| M[Reject Request]
    end

    subgraph Implementation & Monitoring
        J --> N[Publish Decision to Archive OS]
        N --> O[Entity Implements Plan]
        O --> P[Quarterly Progress Reporting]
        P --> Q{Trigger Checks}
        Q --> |Risk Threshold Exceeded| R[Escalation Signal to OVAC]
        Q --> |All Clear| S[Continue Monitoring]
        R --> E
    end

    style Submission & Intake fill:#f9f,stroke:#333,stroke-width:2px
    style Pre-Review Pods fill:#bbf,stroke:#333,stroke-width:2px
    style OVAC Deliberation fill:#bfb,stroke:#333,stroke-width:2px
    style Decision Outcome fill:#ffb,stroke:#333,stroke-width:2px
    style Implementation & Monitoring fill:#fbf,stroke:#333,stroke-width:2px
```

---

## üß† **Workflow Interpretation (Step-by-Step)**

### **1Ô∏è‚É£ Submission & Intake**

* Entity submits a proposal via the governance portal.
* The system verifies completeness; incomplete proposals are returned with structured feedback.

**Artifacts generated:**

```
ovac.request.created
ovac.request.metadata
```

---

### **2Ô∏è‚É£ Pre-Review Pods**

* Each pod evaluates the request and produces structured signals and artifacts.

  * Identity (permission to act)
  * Legitimacy (Ubuntuwa)
  * Financial risk (Uhuru)
  * Human impact (Moyo)
  * Continuity risk
  * Compliance flags

**Artifacts generated:**

```
identity.validation.artifact
legitimacy.score
financial.risk.report
human.impact.index
continuity.readiness.map
compliance.status.artifact
```

These are assembled into a **Review Packet**.

---

### **3Ô∏è‚É£ OVAC Deliberation**

* Review Packet enters a **sleepy consensus window** (asynchronous first).
* If no blocking concerns arise:

  * Consensus is assumed after the set window (e.g., 72 hrs).
* If any blocker arises:

  * A synchronous session is triggered (host entity facilitates).

**Artifacts generated:**

```
ovac.consensus.log
ovac.session.minutes
```

---

### **4Ô∏è‚É£ Decision Execution**

Using the **Decision Table Framework** above, OVAC determines:

* Approve
* Approve with conditions
* Defer
* Reject

**Artifacts generated:**

```
ovac.decision.record
decision.conditions (if any)
```

---

### **5Ô∏è‚É£ Implementation & Monitoring**

* Approved entities begin implementation.
* Progress is regularly reported (quarterly or per schedule).
* Monitoring pipelines check trigger conditions for risk or deviation.

If trigger conditions are met (e.g., budget overrun, risk thresholds crossed), an **escalation signal** routes back into OVAC deliberation.

**Artifacts generated:**

```
implementation.status
quarterly.progress.report
escalation.signal
```

---

## üìö **Artifact-Centric Governance Loop**

Your governance is **artifact-centric**:

* Every step creates artifacts in Archive OS
* DecisionRefs connect signals + decisions
* Bahari Network propagates messages and events
* Pods feed structured analytic signals into OVAC

This makes your governance:
‚úî **Auditable**
‚úî **Reproducible**
‚úî **Traceable**
‚úî **Compliant**
‚úî **Asynchronous + Synchronous as needed**

---

## üß† **How This Scales**

As more coops and ventures join the federation:

* Pods expand or specialize
* Decision tables grow with doctrine
* OVAC workflows remain the same structure
* Entities replay the same lifecycle with increased complexity

The model stays robust because:
üîπ It is **modular**
üîπ It is **signal + artifact driven**
üîπ It uses **machine-readable policies**
üîπ It supports **asynchronous and synchronous governance**

‚úÖ A **workflow automation spec** for Bahari Network events

Here‚Äôs a **practical, federation-aligned schedule of OVAC‚Äôs foundational meetings over a year**, plus a clear rule for **how long OVAC host rotations last** ‚Äî built for your Pamoja governance model.

---

# üúÇ **OVAC Foundational Meeting Cadence (Yearly)**

OVAC is a **part-time parliament** ‚Äî it does *not meet constantly* like a corporate board. Instead, it runs on a **predictable yearly rhythm** with defined meeting types, purposes, and deliverables.

Each meeting type is tied to a **decision lifecycle stage** (intake, review, approval, monitoring) and produces **Archive OS artifacts**.

---

## üìÖ **1) Annual Strategy Kickoff**

**When:** Year Start (e.g., Month 1)
**Duration:** Full day (remote + in-person hybrid)
**Purpose:**
‚úî Align OVAC members on doctrine refresh
‚úî Approve annual strategic priorities, risk frameworks, KPI targets
‚úî Set host rotation transitions if applicable
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.strategy.kickoff.record`
* `ovac.doctrine.update`
* `annual.priority.artifact`

---

## üìÜ **2) Quarterly Foundational Review (x4)**

**When:** Every ~3 months (Ends of Q1, Q2, Q3, Q4)
**Duration:** 2-4 hours each
**Purpose:**
‚úî Review progress on previously approved items
‚úî Assess quarterly risk & legitimacy dashboards
‚úî Update decision table thresholds if needed
‚úî Validate continuity readiness signals
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.quarterly.review.record`
* `quarterly.kpi.artifact`

---

## üóÇ **3) Intake & Triage Cadence (Ongoing Weekly)**

**When:** Weekly or Bi-weekly
**Duration:** 60‚Äì90 minutes
**Purpose:**
‚úî Triage new submissions
‚úî Assign pods for pre-review
‚úî Distribute decision packets
‚úî Update request queue status
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.intake.sync.log`
* `ovac.request.triage.artifact`

---

## üß† **4) Sleeper Consensus Windows (Asynchronous, Ongoing)**

**When:** Continuous (for proposals triggered)
**Duration:** Consensus window (e.g., 48‚Äì72 hrs)
**Purpose:**
‚úî Asynchronously close out routine approvals via sleepy consensus
‚úî Capture tacit support or concerns
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.consensus.log`

*No live meeting needed unless there‚Äôs a blocking risk.*

---

## üîé **5) Ad Hoc Risk Escalation Sessions**

**When:** On trigger (risk, shock event, compliance breach)
**Duration:** 1‚Äì2 hours or more
**Purpose:**
‚úî Assess emergent threat or deviation
‚úî Decide on mitigation paths
‚úî Issue escalation decisions
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.escalation.record`

Triggers are coded in decision tables like:

```
IF (financial.risk > threshold) OR (legitimacy < threshold)
  THEN trigger risk session
```

---

## üìä **6) Mid-Year Governance Calibration**

**When:** Mid-Year (e.g., Month 6)
**Duration:** Half-day intensive
**Purpose:**
‚úî Deep review of doctrine, host rotation readiness
‚úî Rebalance priorities and risk models
‚úî Review host performance and continuity patterns
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.midyear.calibration.artifact`

---

## üì¶ **7) Post-Implementation Reviews (PIR)**

**When:** After major program execution cycles
**Duration:** 1‚Äì2 hours per PIR
**Purpose:**
‚úî Evaluate outcomes vs decisions
‚úî Produce lessons learned
‚úî Update decision tables
**Artifacts:**

* `post_implementation.review`
* `lesson.learned.artifact`

---

## üß† **8) Host Transition Ceremony**

**When:** At end of host rotation period
**Duration:** ~2 hours
**Purpose:**
‚úî Handoff of OVAC responsibilities to next host
‚úî Archive host performance report
‚úî Archive OS continuity handoff
**Artifacts:**

* `ovac.host.transition.record`

---

# üìä **Year-In-The-Life OVAC Calendar (Example)**

| Month  | Meeting / Activity                               |
| ------ | ------------------------------------------------ |
| **1**  | Annual Strategy Kickoff                          |
| **2**  | Weekly Intake Sync                               |
| **3**  | Quarterly Review (Q1)                            |
| **4**  | Weekly Intake Sync + Sleeper Consensus           |
| **5**  | Ongoing Intake Sync / Risk Sessions              |
| **6**  | Mid-Year Governance Calibration                  |
| **7**  | Weekly Intake Sync                               |
| **8**  | Quarterly Review (Q2)                            |
| **9**  | Ongoing Intake Sync / PIR                        |
| **10** | Weekly Intake Sync                               |
| **11** | Quarterly Review (Q3)                            |
| **12** | Quarterly Review (Q4) + Host Transition Ceremony |

This cadence balances **predictable governance rhythms** with **responsive oversight**.

---

# üîÅ **OVAC Host Rotation ‚Äî Length & Rules**

OVAC host rotation is part of your governance design and ensures that **no single entity permanently dominates governance infrastructure**.

### **Host Rotation Duration**

**Standard Host Term:**
üìç **6 months** (preferred for agility + experience)

**Alternative / Optional Term:**
üìç **12 months** ‚Äî for deeper continuity in early federation days

**Important:**
Term lengths can be codified in your decision tables as governance doctrine.

---

## üß† **Host Term Rules**

### üü° **Staggered Rotation**

* Two hosts overlap briefly at rotation boundaries to ensure continuity
* Transitions occur during the **Host Transition Ceremony**

### üü° **Host Charter Responsibilities**

Each host entity must:
‚úî Provide secretariat operations
‚úî Maintain governance infrastructure (Archive OS, Bahari endpoints)
‚úî Facilitate meeting logistics
‚úî Coordinate artifact publication
‚úî Manage intake queues and dashboards
‚úî Liaise with pods for pre-reviews
‚úî Maintain performance & continuity logs

Charter artifacts:

```
ovac.host.charter
ovac.host.performance.report
```

### üü° **Host Selection Criteria**

* Prior rotation order
* Entity capability to provide secretariat services
* Member class diversity
* Risk neutrality (no dominance by one entity class)

You can write a *host rotation decision table* such as:

```
IF next.year.start
  THEN assign next.host.in.rotation.sequence
```

---

# üß† **What Host Rotation Means Operationally**

When an entity hosts OVAC:

### **Day 1 of Host Term**

* Host provisions infrastructure ( portals, UI, APIs )
* Host archives baseline governance artifacts
* Host onboards delegates and synchronizes access

### **Throughout Term**

* Host runs weekly intake syncs
* Host schedules foundational quarterly reviews
* Host ensures pods‚Äô artifact workflows are connected
* Host runs sleepy consensus monitoring
* Host prepares quarterly reports

### **End of Term**

* Host conducts Host Transition Ceremony
* Host produces performance & continuity artifacts
* Host hands over governance namespace to new host

---

# üìå **How the Rotation Pattern Folds Into Your Federation Model**

Given your Ashe cycle and federation build pattern:

1. **Early Stage (Kernel, OVCS, Kumba)**

   * OVAC host may be your personal office or Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA Coalition
   * Shorter rotation (6 months) is advisable for experimentation

2. **Growth Stage (More Coops Join)**

   * Hosts rotate among mid-tier coops (Uhuru, Moyo, Bahari, etc.)
   * Host durability ensures governance demands don‚Äôt overwhelm any single entity

3. **Mature Stage (Full Federation)**

   * Hosts rotate predictably
   * Performance reviews influence future rotation priority

---

# üß† **How Your Governance Tools Use This Cadence**

Each foundational meeting (and host rotation moment) should produce artifacts in Archive OS such as:

* `ovac.strategy.kickoff.record`
* `ovac.quarterly.review.artifact`
* `ovac.consensus.log`
* `ovac.decision.record`
* `host.performance.report`
* `ovac.host.transition.record`

These artifacts are then:
‚úî Linked to decisionRefs
‚úî Fed into Bahari Network alerts
‚úî Indexed for audit queries
‚úî Used to adjust decision tables

Absolutely ‚Äî here‚Äôs a **decision table specification for OVAC Host Selection and Rotation** designed to be *executable*, *doctrinally consistent*, and *integrated with your federation governance logic* (Archive OS + Bahari + decision engine).

You can implement this as JSON/CSV/DSL logic in your decision engine.

# üßæ **OVAC Host Selection & Rotation Decision Table**

This table determines:

‚úÖ Which entity should *host OVAC* next
‚úÖ When the rotation should occur
‚úÖ Whether the rotation is permitted based on readiness & compliance

It uses inputs from governance state (entities, readiness, escrow, rotation history) and outputs:

üëâ Next host entity
üëâ Rotation schedule
üëâ Conditions required before activation
üëâ Artifacts to emit

---

## üìä **Decision Table: OVAC Host Selection**

| **Rule ID** | **Last Host**      | **Rotation Overdue** | **Entity Readiness** | **Entity Compliance Status** | **Entity Hosting Load Factor** | **Outcome: Next Host**     | **Conditions / Notes**                                         |
| ----------- | ------------------ | -------------------- | -------------------- | ---------------------------- | ------------------------------ | -------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------- |
| H1          | Any                | No                   | High                 | PASS                         | Low                            | **Stay with Current Host** | Rotation deferred until end of term                            |
| H2          | Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA   | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Normal                         | **Uhuru Credit Union**     | Normal rotation progression                                    |
| H3          | Uhuru Credit Union | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Normal                         | **Moyo Collective**        | Normal rotation progression                                    |
| H4          | Moyo Collective    | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Normal                         | **Bahari Network**         | Normal rotation progression                                    |
| H5          | Bahari Network     | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Normal                         | **Ubunye Engineering**     | Normal rotation progression                                    |
| H6          | Ubunye Engineering | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Normal                         | **Umoya Society**          | Normal rotation progression                                    |
| H7          | Umoya Society      | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Normal                         | **Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA**       | Loop back around                                               |
| H8          | Any                | Yes                  | Low                  | FAIL                         | ‚Äî                              | **Hold Rotation**          | Host candidacy must fix readiness / compliance before rotating |
| H9          | Any                | Yes                  | High                 | FAIL                         | ‚Äî                              | **Defer Rotation**         | Entity must pass compliance check first                        |
| H10         | Any                | Yes                  | Normal               | PASS                         | High                           | **Skip Entity**            | If hosting load factor is high, skip to next                   |
| H11         | Any                | Yes                  | High                 | PASS                         | Low                            | **Next in Rotation Order** | Baseline case                                                  |

---

## üß† **Input Definitions (Used in Logic)**

| **Input Field**                | **Meaning**                                           | **Source**                                  |
| ------------------------------ | ----------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------- |
| **Last Host**                  | The entity that last hosted OVAC                      | Archive OS & rotation log                   |
| **Rotation Overdue**           | Boolean indicating rotation schedule has matured      | Decision engine (time calendar)             |
| **Entity Readiness**           | Whether entity has required infrastructure + maturity | Entity scorecard (Archive OS, pod feedback) |
| **Entity Compliance Status**   | Whether entity is compliant with federation policies  | Compliance pod artifact                     |
| **Entity Hosting Load Factor** | Relative hosting burden (past frequency/overlap)      | Host history dashboard                      |

**Readiness** is based on:

* Artifact infrastructure
* Secretariat capability
* Identity & role fabric connected
* Bahari endpoint stability

**Compliance Status** ensures:

* All governance artifacts are correct
* No unresolved audit issues
* No sanctions

**Hosting Load Factor** manages fairness:

* Entities with too many rotations recently get temporarily skipped

---

## üß† **Field Thresholds & Value Options**

### **1. Rotation Overdue**

* TRUE ‚Üí Next in order can be selected
* FALSE ‚Üí Current host stays

### **2. Entity Readiness**

* **High** ‚Üí Fully capable
* **Normal** ‚Üí Minor improvements needed (still acceptable)
* **Low** ‚Üí Not ready

### **3. Compliance Status**

* **PASS** ‚Üí Compliant with federation policy
* **FAIL** ‚Üí Missing compliance signals

### **4. Hosting Load Factor**

* **Low** ‚Üí Underutilized host
* **Normal** ‚Üí Balanced
* **High** ‚Üí Recently hosted, skip

---

## üìå **Rotation Order Logic**

The rotation order is explicit:

1. **Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA**
2. **Uhuru Credit Union**
3. **Moyo Collective**
4. **Bahari Network**
5. **Ubunye Engineering**
6. **Umoya Society**
7. **Back to Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA**

This list can be expanded as new entities join.

# üß† **Decision Table Rule Mapping (Executable Form)**

Here‚Äôs a JSON-like pseudocode version you can import into your decision engine:

```json
[
 {
  "ruleId": "H1",
  "conditions": {
    "rotationOverdue": false
  },
  "outcome": {
    "nextHost": "CurrentHost",
    "action": "Defer Rotation",
    "notes": "Rotation not due"
  }
 },
 {
  "ruleId": "H2",
  "conditions": {
    "lastHost": "Ubuntuwa-ZULAMBA",
    "rotationOverdue": true,
    "entityReadiness": "High",
    "entityComplianceStatus": "PASS",
    "hostingLoadFactor": "Normal"
  },
  "outcome": {
    "nextHost": "Uhuru Credit Union",
    "action": "Rotate",
    "notes": "Standard rotation"
  }
 },
 {
  "ruleId": "H8",
  "conditions": {
    "rotationOverdue": true,
    "entityReadiness": "Low"
  },
  "outcome": {
    "nextHost": "Hold",
    "action": "Hold Rotation",
    "notes": "Entity not ready to host"
  }
 },
 {
  "ruleId": "H10",
  "conditions": {
    "rotationOverdue": true,
    "entityReadiness": "Normal",
    "entityComplianceStatus": "PASS",
    "hostingLoadFactor": "High"
  },
  "outcome": {
    "nextHost": "SkipEntity",
    "action": "Skip and pick next",
    "notes": "High hosting load factor"
  }
 },
 {
  "ruleId": "H11",
  "conditions": {
    "rotationOverdue": true,
    "entityReadiness": "High",
    "entityComplianceStatus": "PASS",
    "hostingLoadFactor": "Low"
  },
  "outcome": {
    "nextHost": "NextEntityInRotation",
    "action": "Rotate",
    "notes": "Default accept"
  }
 }
]
```

> You can expand this table with more entity types, parity rules, and adaptive weights (e.g., a rotation penalty for recent hosts).

---

# üß† **Example Scenario**

### **Context**

* Last host: Moyo Collective
* Rotation is due
* Next in sequence: Bahari Network
* Bahari is compliant & ready
* Bahari has low hosting load

**Evaluation Path:**

1. Check `rotationOverdue` ‚Üí TRUE
2. Evaluate readiness ‚Üí HIGH
3. Evaluate compliance ‚Üí PASS
4. Evaluate load ‚Üí LOW
5. Default ‚Üí Rule `H11` ‚Üí **Bahari Network** becomes next host

**Action:**

```
ovac.host.assignment.artifact
{
  nextHost: "Bahari Network",
  rotationEffectiveDate: "2026-01-01",
  conditions: []
}
```

---

## üß† **Hosting Load Factor Example Logic**

You may also set a *dynamic load factor* rule, such as:

```sql
IF hostCount(past 3 cycles) >= 2
THEN hostingLoadFactor = "High"
```

This prevents the same entity from hosting too often.

---

# üß† **Host Compliance & Readiness Checks**

Before the rotation finalizes, check:

‚úî Entity‚Äôs compliance summary
‚úî Secretariat readiness status
‚úî Archival namespace availability
‚úî API endpoints (Bahari) live
‚úî Scheduled ceremonial handoff window

If any of these fail, rule `H8` or `H9` engages, and rotation is deferred until compliance.

## üß† **Decision Table Integration with OVAC Workflows**

This table is used in a **pre-meeting stage**:

üö© At Rotation Interval Trigger ‚Üí
‚Ü™ Decision Engine runs Host Selection Table ‚Üí
‚Ü™ Generates `ovac.host.assignment` ‚Üí
‚Ü™ Archive OS persists artifact ‚Üí
‚Ü™ Federation Service Council confirms ‚Üí
‚Ü™ Host Transition Ceremony scheduled

This ensures talk isn‚Äôt just theoretical ‚Äî it‚Äôs **artifact-driven and executable**.

# üúÇ **Sankofa Council ‚Äî The Pamoja Federation Meta-Board**

**The Sankofa Council** is your federation‚Äôs **strategic governance body** ‚Äî essentially the federation-level board of oversight, alignment, risk moderation, and doctrinal authority. It serves the same functional role as OVAC in all governance workflows, but now under the name that reflects both *ancestral wisdom* and *forward-looking oversight*.

üîπ *Sankofa* ‚Äî a concept from Akan philosophy meaning ‚Äúto go back and get it,‚Äù symbolizing the practice of learning from the past to inform the present and future.

Thus, the **Sankofa Council** embodies the idea that your governance integrates:

* **Historical context**
* **Federated values**
* **Legitimate community intelligence**
* **Strategic foresight and continuity**

| Decision record        | **sankofa.decision.record**           |
| Implementation request | **sankofa.request.record**            |
| Quarterly review       | **sankofa.quarterly.review.artifact** |

---

# üß† Sankofa Delegates (Member Lifecycle)

Delegate lifecycle artifacts now become:

```
sankofa.delegate.nomination
sankofa.delegate.onboarding
sankofa.delegate.transition
sankofa.delegate.alumni.record
```

# üìà Sankofa Governance Decision Flow

Workflow steps with new naming:

1. **Entity Submission** ‚Üí sankofa.request.created
2. **Pod Pre-Review** ‚Üí legitimacy, identity, finance, human impact artifacts
3. **Sankofa Deliberation** ‚Üí sleepy consensus log
4. **Decision** ‚Üí sankofa.decision.record
5. **Implementation Oversight** ‚Üí sankofa.implementation.status
6. **Post-Implementation Review** ‚Üí sankofa.postImplementation.review

The logic and cadence remain consistent ‚Äî only the governance brand shifts to **Sankofa Council**.

## üß† **HOW THESE TABLES FIT TOGETHER**

Your Sankofa Council governance engine will typically evaluate tables in this order:

1. **Compliance Gate Table** ‚Äî can we proceed at all?
2. **Identity & Authority Table** ‚Äî does the requester have rights?
3. **Legitimacy Table** ‚Äî does the broader community support it?
4. **Financial Risk Table** ‚Äî is it fiscally viable?
5. **Human Systems Impact Table** ‚Äî what‚Äôs the human effect?
6. **Continuity Table** ‚Äî does it threaten continuity?
7. **Strategic Request Approval Table** ‚Äî final decision matrix
8. **Risk Escalation Table** ‚Äî at any step, triggers escalate

Each table produces an artifact (e.g., `compliance.status`, `legitimacy.status`, `financial.status`, `human.impact.status`, `continuity.status`) that becomes part of a **decision packet** fed into the final ‚ÄúStrategic Request Approval‚Äù table.

---

## üß† **IMPLEMENTATION NOTES**

* Tables should be deployed as **executable decision rules** in your decision engine (JSON, DSL, no-code workflow, database rules).
* **DecisionRefs** link table results to artifacts stored in *Archive OS*.
* All tables must support **logging + audit** ‚Äî each decision should capture:

  ```
  ruleId, inputs, outcome, decisionRef
  ```
* These tables can be independently versioned and updated as doctrine evolves.
* Use **sleepy consensus** to confirm changes in tables or thresholds.

---

## üß† **ARTIFACT NAMING CONVENTIONS**

Each table‚Äôs output becomes part of a Sankofa artifact:

* `sankofa.compliance.result`
* `sankofa.identity.validation`
* `sankofa.legitimacy.score`
* `sankofa.financial.assessment`
* `sankofa.human.impact.index`
* `sankofa.continuity.readiness`
* `sankofa.risk.escalation.signal`
* `sankofa.decision.record`

These are archived and referenced via decisionRefs.

---

## üìÅ **1) Artifact Schema Definitions for the *Jiwe Archives***

*(Jiwe = the immutable, canonical source of truth for governance artifacts ‚Äî formerly ‚ÄúArchive OS‚Äù)*

These schemas define **how governance data is structured, stored, and referenced** in the Jiwe Archives so that Sankofa Council logic, pods, and decision engines can reliably read/write artifacts with consistency and auditability.

---

### üßæ **Core Artifact Types (Base Schema)**

> All artifacts share a set of **common metadata fields** plus **type-specific fields**.

#### **Common Metadata (All Artifacts)**

```json5
{
  "artifactId": "string",             // Unique Jiwe identifier
  "artifactType": "string",           // e.g., "sankofa.decision.record"
  "createdBy": "string",              // Identity UID of creator
  "createdAt": "timestamp",           // ISO 8601 UTC
  "refs": ["artifactId"],             // Cross-artifact references
  "decisionRef": "string|null",       // Link to Sankofa decision if relevant
  "tags": ["string"],                 // Optional semantic tags
  "version": "integer",               // Version for revision history
  "signature": "string"               // Cryptographic signature for immutability
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.request.record**

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.request.record",
  "requestId": "string",                // Unique request ID
  "entitySponsor": "string",            // Entity UID that submitted
  "requestSchema": "string",            // Type of request ("investment","policyChange", etc.)
  "payload": { ... },                   // The actual request body
  "status": "string",                   // "pending" | "triaged" | "reviewed"
  "createdAt": "...",
  "refs": []
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.preReview.report**

Generated by pods during pre-review.

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.preReview.report",
  "requestId": "string",                // Linked to sankofa.request.record
  "pod": "string",                      // "identity", "legitimacy", etc.
  "assessment": "pass|warn|fail",
  "details": { ... },                   // Pod-specific signals
  "priority": "low|medium|high"
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.decision.record**

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.decision.record",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "requestId": "string",                // Linked request
  "decisionOutcome": "approve|defer|reject|conditional",
  "conditions": { ... },                // If conditional
  "rationale": "string",                // Human summary
  "appliedDecisionTable": "string",     // Decision table version/name
  "results": {
    "signals": { ... },                 // Consolidated pod signals
    "tableOutcome": "ruleId"
  },
  "approvedBy": ["string"],             // Sankofa delegate identity UIDs
  "decisionAt": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.consensus.log**

For asynchronous ‚Äúsleepy consensus‚Äù tracking:

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.consensus.log",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "votes": [
    {
      "delegateUID": "string",
      "vote": "support|conditional|object|abstain",
      "timestamp": "timestamp"
    }
  ],
  "consensusReached": "boolean",
  "consensusOutcome": "string",
  "closedAt": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.host.assignment**

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.host.assignment",
  "hostEntity": "string",               // Entity UID
  "termStart": "timestamp",
  "termEnd": "timestamp",
  "hostCharterArtifact": "artifactId",  // Link to charter
  "rotationRuleApplied": "string"       // e.g., "H2"
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.host.transition.record**

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.host.transition.record",
  "fromHost": "string",
  "toHost": "string",
  "transitionAt": "timestamp",
  "handoverNotes": "string",
  "validationArtifacts": ["artifactId"]
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.implementation.status**

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.implementation.status",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "reportedBy": "string",               // Entity UID
  "phase": "string",                    // e.g., "Q1", "milestone1"
  "status": "onTrack|delayed|completed",
  "issues": [ ... ],
  "progressDetails": { ... },
  "updatedAt": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üßæ **Artifact: sankofa.postImplementation.review**

```json5
{
  "artifactType": "sankofa.postImplementation.review",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "reviewedAt": "timestamp",
  "results": { ... },
  "lessonsLearned": "string",
  "updatesToDoctrine": ["decisionTableName"]
}
```

---

## üß† **Schema Principles**

‚úî **Immutable:** Stored in Jiwe Archives and cryptographically signed
‚úî **Linked:** Connected via `refs` & `decisionRef`
‚úî **Queryable:** Structured for federation dashboards
‚úî **Traceable:** Every change/version is logged

---

## üì° **2) Bahari Event Contract Spec for Decision Table Triggers**

The **Bahari Network** delivers event-driven messages between systems (entities, pods, Sankofa Council engine, Jiwe Archives, dashboards). You can implement this with an event bus or federated message layer.

Here is the **contract spec** ‚Äî what events exist, what payloads they carry, and what triggers they respond to.

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/requests**

**Emitted by:** Submission interfaces, entities
**Consumed by:** Intake/triage services, Sankofa preprocessors

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_REQUEST_CREATED",
  "requestId": "string",
  "entitySponsor": "string",
  "requestSchema": "string",
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/preReview**

**Emitted by:** Pods after assessment
**Consumed by:** Sankofa decision preprocessor

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_PRE_REVIEW_COMPLETED",
  "requestId": "string",
  "pod": "string",
  "assessment": "pass|warn|fail",
  "artifactId": "string",       // sankofa.preReview.report
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/consensus**

**Emitted by:** Sankofa consensus engine
**Consumed by:** Decision engine, dashboards

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_CONSENSUS_UPDATE",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "voteUpdate": {
    "delegateUID": "string",
    "vote": "support|conditional|object|abstain"
  },
  "currentStatus": "string",    // draft|consensusAchieved|blocked
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/decision**

**Emitted by:** Sankofa decision engine
**Consumed by:** Entities, monitoring dashboards, Jiwe Archives

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_DECISION_ISSUED",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "outcome": "approve|defer|reject|conditional",
  "conditions": { ... },
  "artifactId": "string",       // sankofa.decision.record
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/hostRotation**

**Emitted by:** Sankofa host selection logic
**Consumed by:** Federation Service Council, entities

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_HOST_ROTATION",
  "previousHost": "string",
  "nextHost": "string",
  "artifactId": "string",       // sankofa.host.assignment
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/implementationUpdate**

**Emitted by:** Entities reporting progress
**Consumed by:** Sankofa monitoring, dashboards

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_IMPLEMENTATION_STATUS",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "status": "onTrack|delayed|completed",
  "artifactId": "string",      // sankofa.implementation.status
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

### üõ∞ **Event Channel: bahari://sankofa/riskTrigger**

**Emitted by:** Risk engines / pods
**Consumed by:** Sankofa escalation logic

```json5
{
  "eventType": "SANKOFA_RISK_TRIGGER",
  "decisionId": "string",
  "riskType": "financial|human|continuity|compliance",
  "details": { ... },
  "timestamp": "timestamp"
}
```

---

## üß† **Event Contract Notes**

‚úî **Each event must include a timestamp and unique IDs**
‚úî **Payloads are minimal and reference artifact IDs** so decision engines can fetch full data from the Jiwe Archives
‚úî **Namespaces reflect Sankofa domains** for filtering and subscription
‚úî **Events are idempotent** ‚Äî repeated events do not create duplicates

---

## üì° **Event Subscription Map**

| Subscriber       | Subscribes To                 | Action                    |
| ---------------- | ----------------------------- | ------------------------- |
| Sankofa Intake   | SANKOFA_REQUEST_CREATED       | Generate triage artifacts |
| Pod Services     | SANKOFA_REQUEST_CREATED       | Pre-review outputs        |
| Consensus Engine | SANKOFA_PRE_REVIEW_COMPLETED  | Update vote packets       |
| Decision Engine  | SANKOFA_CONSENSUS_UPDATE      | Finalize decisions        |
| Dashboards       | SANKOFA_DECISION_ISSUED       | Update UI                 |
| Monitoring       | SANKOFA_IMPLEMENTATION_STATUS | KPI tracking              |
| Risk Escalation  | SANKOFA_RISK_TRIGGER          | Trigger escalation        |

---

## üß† **Contract Semantics (Key Terms)**

**eventType** ‚Äì Canonical event identifier
**artifactId** ‚Äì Link to the Jiwe Archive artifact
**decisionId / requestId** ‚Äì Correlates events to workflows
**timestamp** ‚Äì UTC(ISO 8601) for ordering and audits

---

## üß† **Putting It Into Practice**

1. **Entity submits request** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_REQUEST_CREATED*
2. **Pods review feeds** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_PRE_REVIEW_COMPLETED* events
3. **Consensus updates** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_CONSENSUS_UPDATE*
4. **Decision finalized** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_DECISION_ISSUED*
5. **Host rotations change** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_HOST_ROTATION*
6. **Implementations report status** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_IMPLEMENTATION_STATUS*
7. **Risk triggers push escalation** ‚Üí *SANKOFA_RISK_TRIGGER*

All events are logged and available to subscribers and boards via Bahari.

üìå A **message/event sequence chart (Mermaid)** for the Sankofa lifecycle
üìå A **sample JSON HTTP API contract** based on Bahari events
üìå A **dashboard schema** for monitoring artifacts & signals

Just tell me which you want!

Absolutely ‚Äî and this is a **great clarifying statement** for how the *Jiwe Archives* (your federation‚Äôs canonical archival system) is meant to function.

Here‚Äôs a **precise and formal definition** you can use in your governance docs, artifact schemas, and system plans:

---

## üìÅ **Jiwe Archives ‚Äî The Source of All Truth**

**The Jiwe Archives** is the federation‚Äôs **immutable, canonical, system-wide archive** of:

### üìå 1. **Artifact Libraries**

Structured, typed artifacts representing:

* Decisions
* Requests
* Reviews
* Plans & proposals
* Pod outputs
* Governance signals
* Metrics snapshots
* Narrative artifacts
* Identity and authority logs

These are stored as **typed objects** with schemas (e.g., `sankofa.decision.record`, `sankofa.request.record`) and linked via **refs / decisionRefs**.

---

### üìå 2. **Ledgers**

Chronological, **audit-ready logs of events and state changes**, including:

* Request submissions
* Pod assessments
* Consensus updates
* Decisions issued
* Host rotations
* Implementation status changes
* Risk escalations
* Compliance checks

These ledgers provide **tamper-evident chronology** for:

* Audits
* Governance reviews
* Continuity planning
* Legal/regulatory evidence
* Forensic analysis

Each ledger entry is a **Jiwe artifact** with:

* Timestamp
* Signature
* Identity UID
* DecisionRef linkages

---

## üß† **What Jiwe Contains**

The Jiwe Archives includes:

### üìå **a) Artifact Libraries**

Collections of typed artifacts, organized by domain:

| Library                    | Artifact Type Prefix                 |
| -------------------------- | ------------------------------------ |
| Sankofa Council Governance | `sankofa.*`                          |
| Pod Outputs                | `*.preReview.report`, `*.analysis.*` |
| Entity Submissions         | `*.request.record`                   |
| Implementation Status      | `*.implementation.status`            |
| Continuity & Succession    | `*.continuity.*`                     |
| Compliance Artifacts       | `*.compliance.*`                     |
| Identity/Authority Logs    | `member.*`, `role.*`                 |
| Narrative & Legitimacy     | `narrative.*`, `legitimacy.*`        |
| Financial & Risk           | `financial.*`, `risk.*`              |
| Host Rotation              | `sankofa.host.*`                     |

> These form **libraries** ‚Äî indexed collections of artifacts that can be queried, referenced, and audited.

---

### üìå **b) Ledgers**

Chronological records of all key events, such as:

* **Request Ledger**

  ```
  sankofa.request.record
  ```

* **Decision Ledger**

  ```
  sankofa.decision.record
  ```

* **Consensus Ledger**

  ```
  sankofa.consensus.log
  ```

* **Host Rotation Ledger**

  ```
  sankofa.host.transition.record
  ```

* **Implementation Status Ledger**

  ```
  sankofa.implementation.status
  ```

These ledgers are **ordered timelines** that reflect *everything that occurred within the federation‚Äôs governance flows*.

---

## üìú **How Jiwe Archives Works With Governance**

Every governance action ‚Äî whether it‚Äôs a pod output, Sankofa Council decision, escalation signal, or implementation update ‚Äî is:

### üîπ **Captured as an Artifact**

Using one of the Jiwe schemas (defined earlier).

### üîπ **Linked via Refs**

Artifacts link to each other:

```
artifact.refs = [otherArtifactId, ...]
decisionRef = sankofa.decision.record.artifactId
```

This enables **artifact graphs** for:

* lineage
* traceability
* impact analysis

---

### üîπ **Signed & Immutable**

Each artifact has:

* cryptographic signature
* version
* timestamp
  ensuring **non-repudiation and audit integrity**.

You can query:

* ‚ÄúShow all governance actions for Decision X‚Äù
* ‚ÄúList all risk escalations tied to Request Y‚Äù
* ‚ÄúReconstruct the lifecycle of Host Rotation Z‚Äù

---

## üß† **Jiwe vs Traditional Archives**

| Feature                             | Traditional Archive | Jiwe Archives                       |
| ----------------------------------- | ------------------- | ----------------------------------- |
| Mutable?                            | Yes                 | **Immutable**                       |
| Traceable on chain?                 | Not necessarily     | **Yes, cryptographically verified** |
| Linked artifacts?                   | Manual              | **Ref-driven artifact graph**       |
| Queryable for lineage?              | Hard                | **Designed for lineage + audit**    |
| Integrated with governance engines? | No                  | **Yes (decision tables + events)**  |
| Integrated with federation events?  | No                  | **Yes via Bahari event contracts**  |

---

## üîó **How Jiwe Interacts with Bahari Events**

Every Bahari event (e.g., `SANKOFA_REQUEST_CREATED`) results in:

1. An artifact written to Jiwe
2. Chronology appended to relevant ledger(s)
3. A ref linkage back to related artifacts
4. A signal used by decision engines

Thus Jiwe is **both the historical record and the data source** for next-stage governance evaluation.

---

## üß† **What Happens When Something Is Updated?**

Because artifacts are immutable:

‚úî A new artifact *version* is created
‚úî Old version stays in the ledger
‚úî Version history is preserved
‚úî Decision tables reference specific versions via decisionRefs

Example:

```
{
  artifactId: "abc123",
  artifactType: "sankofa.decision.record",
  version: 2,
  prevVersion: "xyz789"
}
```

This enables **ledger-style history and traceability** for all governance data.

---

## üìà **Queryable Dimensions of Jiwe**

You can slice Jiwe Archives by:

| Dimension          | Query Example                         |
| ------------------ | ------------------------------------- |
| By Request         | All artifacts for requestId           |
| By Decision        | All artifacts linked to decisionRef   |
| By Pod             | All legitimacy artifacts in timeframe |
| By Entity          | All submissions from entity           |
| By Host Term       | All events during host term           |
| By Risk Escalation | All risk events with severity         |
| By Member          | All actions by a delegate             |

**In functional terms, Jiwe is:**

üìå A **data lake** for governance
üìå A **ledger of record** for actions
üìå A **graph database** of artifact links
üìå An **audit trail** for decisions
üìå A **data source** for analytics and risk models

All Jiwe artifacts are named with:

```
<domain>.<artifactPurpose>.<status/version>
```

Examples:

```
sankofa.request.record
sankofa.decision.record.v2
sankofa.consensus.log
identity.profile.artifact
financial.risk.report
compliance.status.artifact
continuity.readiness.map
```

This naming convention makes it easy to index, search, and reconstruct governance scenarios.

# üìÅ **Jiwe Archives ‚Äî The Distributed Ground-Truth Ledger System**

**The Jiwe Archives** is:
üîπ A **distributed ledger archival system**, not a centralized silo.
üîπ The **single source of truth** across the federation.
üîπ A **master data management system** for governance artifacts, decisions, signals, votes, and state changes.
üîπ Governed by the **Sankofa Council** and maintained cooperatively by **all federation entities**.

‚ÄúJiwe‚Äù literally means **stone** in Swahili ‚Äî symbolizing *foundation, permanence, and enduring truth*.

---

## üß± Core Properties of the Jiwe Archives

### üß† 1. **Distributed Ledger Nature**

* Every participating entity (coops, councils, pods) **runs a node or replica** of Jiwe.
* Consensus protocols ensure **eventual consistency** across all nodes.
* Ledger entries include:

  * Sankofa Council votes & decisions
  * Pod outputs (legitimacy, finance, continuity, identity)
  * Entity submissions
  * Implementation updates
  * Compliance proofs
  * Risk signaling events
  * Host rotation records
* Each ledger entry is **immutable**, **versioned**, and **cryptographically signed**.

This means **no single entity ‚Äúowns‚Äù the Jiwe truth** ‚Äî every entity contributes to, verifies, and maintains the distributed ledger.

---

## üîó 2. **Artifact-Linked Master Data**

Every governance artifact stored in Jiwe has:

‚úî A **unique identifier**
‚úî A **type/category**
‚úî **Refs** linking it to related artifacts
‚úî A **decisionRef** pointing to the definitive governance decision
‚úî A **signature** tying it to the authoring identity
‚úî A **timestamp**

Example artifact types include:

* `sankofa.decision.record`
* `sankofa.consensus.log`
* `sankofa.request.record`
* `identity.profile.artifact`
* `legitimacy.score.artifact`
* `financial.risk.report.artifact`
* `continuity.readiness.map.artifact`

Artifacts are stored in **Jiwe‚Äôs distributed ledger**, making them:

* Cryptographically verified
* Immutable
* Federatedly replicated
* Queryable

This supports **ground-truth queries** like:

> ‚ÄúWhat was the legitimacy score used in Decision X?‚Äù
> ‚ÄúWho voted for Condition Y and when?‚Äù
> ‚ÄúWhat was the continuity readiness at the time of execution?‚Äù

---

## üï∏Ô∏è 3. **Linked Decision Graph**

Artifacts in Jiwe form a **directed graph** of governance provenance:

```
sankofa.request.record
  ‚îî‚îÄ refs ‚Üí sankofa.preReview.report
          ‚îî‚îÄ refs ‚Üí sankofa.decision.record
                  ‚îî‚îÄ refs ‚Üí sankofa.consensus.log
                          ‚îî‚îÄ refs ‚Üí sankofa.implementation.status
```

Every artifact *references others* via the ledger, enabling:
‚úî Full lineage tracking
‚úî Causal analysis
‚úî Audit reconstruction
‚úî Temporal reasoning
‚úî Dependency resolution

This graph is the **ground truth** for every governance action in the federation.

---

# üõ°Ô∏è **Sankofa Council ‚Äî Governance Over the Jiwe Archives**

The **Sankofa Council** is the *active governance authority* for the Jiwe system:

### **Governance Roles**

* **Policy Definition:** Sankofa crafts federation doctrine deciding what gets recorded, how decisions are evaluated, and what signals matter.
* **Schema Authority:** Sankofa ratifies artifact schemas ‚Äî establishing the shape of records in Jiwe.
* **Decision Arbitration:** Sankofa decisions become canonical artifacts in Jiwe (`sankofa.decision.record`).
* **Ledger Governance:** Sankofa sets rules for how risks, compliance flags, and escalations are reflected in the ledger.
* **Continuity Enforcement:** Sankofa ensures continuity artifacts (e.g., succession, host rotation) are committed to Jiwe.
* **Master Data Stewardship:** Sankofa ensures that identity, role, status, and authority artifacts are kept consistent and synchronized.

Sankofa does **not ‚Äúhold the ledger‚Äù exclusively** ‚Äî it *governs the rules by which all ledger entries are created, validated, and applied*.

---

## üîÅ **Distributed Maintenance by Entities**

Every federation entity is a **Jiwe node operator and maintenance agent**:

Entities:

* Maintain their **local replica** of the Jiwe ledger
* Sync with other nodes via **Bahari Network events**
* Participate in **consensus protocols** for ledger replication
* Submit artifacts to Jiwe when they perform actions
* Verify incoming artifacts for validity and integrity

This means:

* No central point of failure
* High fault tolerance
* Cross-entity verification
* Local autonomy with global consistency

# üì° **How Jiwe Integrates with Bahari Event Contracts**

Jiwe Archives is updated through **event-driven contracts** on the Bahari Network ‚Äî ensuring artifacts are distributed seamlessly and consistently.

Events like these cause ledger writes:

| Event Type                      | Causes         | Writes                        |
| ------------------------------- | -------------- | ----------------------------- |
| `SANKOFA_REQUEST_CREATED`       | New request    | sankofa.request.record        |
| `SANKOFA_PRE_REVIEW_COMPLETED`  | Pod outputs    | sankofa.preReview.report      |
| `SANKOFA_CONSENSUS_UPDATE`      | Votes update   | sankofa.consensus.log         |
| `SANKOFA_DECISION_ISSUED`       | Final decision | sankofa.decision.record       |
| `SANKOFA_HOST_ROTATION`         | Host change    | sankofa.host.assignment       |
| `SANKOFA_IMPLEMENTATION_STATUS` | Status update  | sankofa.implementation.status |
| `SANKOFA_RISK_TRIGGER`          | Risk event     | sankofa.risk.signal           |

Each event generates an **artifact** which is appended to the Jiwe distributed ledger.
